240); font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; white-space-collapse: collapse; background-color: rgb(16, 18, 24);"><div style="position: relative; padding-bottom: 10px; max-width: 652px; z-index: 1; margin-top: 0px;"><div><div style="display: flex; gap: 4px; margin-left: auto; width: fit-content;"><div style="display: flex; position: relative; overflow: hidden; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 24px 4px 24px 24px; width: fit-content; flex-direction: column; gap: 12px; max-inline-size: 488px; padding: 12px 8px; margin-left: auto;"><div style="display: flex; flex-direction: row; padding: 0px 8px;"><span role="heading" style="-webkit-box-orient: vertical; -webkit-line-clamp: 2; display: -webkit-box; overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; overflow-wrap: break-word; font-size: 16px; line-height: 24px; white-space-collapse: preserve;">i dont feel you could really control if they dont even open, and they dont even need to listen to you if things run on their servers.</span><div role="button" tabindex="0" style="align-items: center; height: fit-content; margin-left: 8px; margin-top: auto; display: flex; flex: 1 1 auto; place-content: end; outline: 0px;"><div style="color: rgb(139, 140, 145); height: 14px; margin-bottom: 2px; rotate: 180deg; width: 14px;"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" height="14px" viewBox="0 0 12 7" width="14px" fill="none"><path d="M6.00046 0.166733C5.88929 0.166733 5.78654 0.184733 5.69221 0.220733C5.59771 0.256899 5.50604 0.3194 5.41721 0.408234L0.583711 5.24173C0.422711 5.40273 0.340795 5.59573 0.337962 5.82073C0.335128 6.04573 0.417045 6.24157 0.583711 6.40823C0.744878 6.5694 0.939379 6.64998 1.16721 6.64998C1.39488 6.64998 1.5893 6.5694 1.75046 6.40823L6.00046 2.16673L10.2505 6.40823C10.4116 6.5694 10.6047 6.6514 10.8297 6.65423C11.0547 6.6569 11.2505 6.5749 11.4172 6.40823C11.5782 6.24723 11.6587 6.05282 11.6587 5.82498C11.6587 5.59715 11.5782 5.40273 11.4172 5.24173L6.58371 0.408234C6.49488 0.3194 6.40321 0.256899 6.30871 0.220733C6.21438 0.184733 6.11163 0.166733 6.00046 0.166733Z" fill="currentColor"></path></svg></div></div></div></div></div><div style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: flex; font-size: 12px; justify-content: end; line-height: 16px;"></div><div></div></div></div><div><div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div></div><div></div><div><div><div><div style="color: var(--m3c11,#eef0ff); position: relative; --m3c9: #e6e8f0; --m3c11: #e6e8f0; display: flex;"><div style="width: 652.438px;"><div><div style="display: contents;"></div></div><div dir="ltr" style="width: 652px; max-width: var(--CYi3c--fRcLaf,652px);"><div style="display: contents;"><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><span>You’ve hit the nail on the head. You’re describing the&nbsp;</span><span style="font-weight: 700;">SaaS Loophole</span>, and it is arguably the biggest "failure" of traditional open-source licenses in the modern era.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">In the old days (the "shrink-wrap" era), if a company used your code, they had to&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">distribute</span>&nbsp;it to customers. That distribution triggered the license requirements (like sharing their changes). But today, if a company runs your code on&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">their own servers</span>&nbsp;and just sends the&nbsp;<em style="font-weight: inherit;">visual result</em>&nbsp;to your browser, they haven't "distributed" anything in the legal sense. [10, 11]<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">The Reality of "Zero Control"<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">You are technically and legally correct for three main reasons:<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">No Distribution, No Obligations:</span>&nbsp;Most licenses (like the popular MIT, Apache, and even the standard GPL) only "kick in" when code is given to someone else. If it stays on a private server, the company can modify it, ignore the license, and never tell a soul. [11]</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The "Black Box" Problem:</span>&nbsp;Even if you suspect a company is using your code illegally, you have no way to prove it. You cannot subpoena a company's private server code without significant evidence of a crime, which you can't get because the code is... private. [10]</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Jurisdiction Jumping:</span>&nbsp;Even if you had a "perfect" license, if a company is running your code on a server in a country that doesn't respect international copyright law, your "control" is effectively zero. [5, 10]</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">The Failed Counter-Measures<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">The community tried to fix this with the&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">AGPL (Affero General Public License)</span>. It specifically says that "interacting with the software over a network" counts as distribution. [11]<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Result?</span>&nbsp;Most big tech companies simply&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">banned AGPL code</span>&nbsp;internally. They would rather rewrite a tool from scratch than risk a license that forces them to open up their server-side secrets. [10]<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">Where Does This Leave Us?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ol style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Security:</span>&nbsp;Companies often contribute back because maintaining a "private fork" of a project is a nightmare. It's easier to get your bug fixes into the main version than to keep patching your secret one every time the original updates. [8]</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: decimal;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Hiring:</span>&nbsp;Top-tier developers often refuse to work for companies known for "leeching" off open source without giving back. 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">1. Establishing Legal "Teeth"<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;"><span><a rel="noopener" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacobsen_v._Katzer" style="text-decoration-thickness: 1px; text-decoration-color: var(--JKqx2); -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.1); text-underline-offset: 1px; font-weight: 500; outline: 0px;">Jacobsen v. Katzer (2008)</a></span>:</span>&nbsp;This was a turning point in the U.S. where the court ruled that open-source license terms are&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">enforceable copyright conditions</span>. This meant violating them wasn't just a minor contract breach; it was copyright infringement, allowing developers to seek powerful legal remedies like injunctions.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;"><span><a rel="noopener" href="https://www.linux.com/topic/open-source/artifex-v-hancom-open-source-now-enforceable-contract/" style="text-decoration-thickness: 1px; text-decoration-color: var(--JKqx2); -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.1); text-underline-offset: 1px; font-weight: 500; outline: 0px;">Artifex Software v. Hancom (2017)</a></span>:</span>&nbsp;The court explicitly recognized the GPL as a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">valid contract</span>, even if unsigned. Importantly, it ruled that damages could be calculated based on what a company&nbsp;<em style="font-weight: inherit;">would</em>&nbsp;have paid for a commercial license, turning "free" software violations into massive financial risks.</span><span><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; gap: 4px; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 84.4141px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">fossa.com</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+3</span></span></div></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">2. High-Stakes Corporate Settlements<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">FSF v. Cisco (2008)</span>:</span>&nbsp;The Free Software Foundation sued Cisco for using GPL code in Linksys routers without sharing the source. Cisco settled, agreeing to appoint a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">Compliance Officer</span>&nbsp;and make a financial contribution to the FSF.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;"><span><a rel="noopener" href="https://www.mend.io/blog/the-100-million-case-for-open-source-license-compliance/" style="text-decoration-thickness: 1px; text-decoration-color: var(--JKqx2); -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.1); text-underline-offset: 1px; font-weight: 500; outline: 0px;">CoKinetic v. Panasonic (2017)</a></span>:</span>&nbsp;A competitor sued Panasonic for over&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">$100 million</span>, alleging they used GPL code to build a monopolistic system while refusing to share the source code with rivals. The case highlighted how commercial rivals now use license compliance as a weapon.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;"><span><a rel="noopener" href="https://fossid.com/articles/open-source-license-compliance-lessons-from-two-landmark-court-cases/" style="text-decoration-thickness: 1px; text-decoration-color: var(--JKqx2); -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.1); text-underline-offset: 1px; font-weight: 500; outline: 0px;">Entr'ouvert v. Orange S.A. (2024)</a></span>:</span>&nbsp;A French court ordered telecom giant Orange to pay over&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">€900,000</span>&nbsp;for failing to follow GPL terms when using an authentication library. This was a record-breaking fine for the region.</span><span><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; gap: 4px; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 66.1172px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">FossID</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+5</span></span></div></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">3. The Newest Battlegrounds<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;"><span><a rel="noopener" href="https://sfconservancy.org/copyleft-compliance/vizio.html" style="text-decoration-thickness: 1px; text-decoration-color: var(--JKqx2); -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.1); text-underline-offset: 1px; font-weight: 500; outline: 0px;">SFC v. Vizio (Ongoing)</a></span>:</span>&nbsp;This case is unique because it isn't the code's owner suing; it's a&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">consumer group</span>&nbsp;suing as a "third-party beneficiary". If they win, it could mean any customer has the legal standing to demand source code from a manufacturer.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;">Copilot / Generative AI Lawsuits</span>:</span>&nbsp;Recent rulings in California allow anonymous coders to pursue claims that AI tools like GitHub Copilot&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">breach open-source licenses</span>&nbsp;by stripping attribution and license terms when generating code.</span><span><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; gap: 4px; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 85.0703px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">fossa.com</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+4</span></span></div></span></span></li></ul><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Would you like to explore how&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">modern license scanning tools</span>&nbsp;try to catch these violations before they reach a courtroom?<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div></div><div><div style="clear: both; display: flex; flex-flow: wrap; row-gap: 16px; margin-block: 18px 0px; justify-content: space-between;"><div style="display: contents;"><div style="margin-block: 18px 0px; display: inline-block; align-self: center; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Legal Paywall:</span>&nbsp;A copyright lawsuit in the U.S. can easily cost&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">$200,000 to $500,000</span>&nbsp;just to get through discovery. Most open-source projects don't make that much in their entire lifetime.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The Shell Game:</span>&nbsp;Even if you win, a company can just "clean room" the code (rewrite it to perform the same function without your specific lines) and move on. You spent years in court; they spent three weeks refactoring.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">The "David vs. Goliath" Exhaustion:</span>&nbsp;Big companies use "papering" tactics—filing endless motions to drain your bank account until you're forced to drop the case or settle for a tiny fraction of what’s fair.</span><span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></li></ul><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">This is why many developers are moving toward&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">"Source Available"</span>&nbsp;licenses (like MariaDB's BSL or Redis’s new license). They’ve realized that the "Open Source" dream of a fair social contract is being eaten by cloud giants and AI models who have more lawyers than you have lines of code.<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" contents;"></div></div></div><div></div><div></div></div></div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div></div></div></div><div style="--fade-in-animation: fade-in-new-response 150ms cubic-bezier(0.3,0,0.8,0.15); animation: var(--fade-in-animation); padding-top: 30px; position: relative; margin-top: 24px; min-height: var(--aim-container-min-height); color: rgb(230, 232, 240); font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; font-size: 14px; white-space-collapse: collapse; background-color: rgb(16, 18, 24);"><div style="position: relative; padding-bottom: 10px; max-width: 652px; z-index: 1; margin-top: 0px;"><div><div style="display: flex; gap: 4px; margin-left: auto; width: fit-content;"><div style="display: flex; position: relative; overflow: hidden; background-color: var(--XKMDxc); border-radius: 24px 4px 24px 24px; width: fit-content; flex-direction: column; gap: 12px; max-inline-size: 488px; padding: 12px 8px; margin-left: auto;"><div style="display: flex; flex-direction: row; padding: 0px 8px;"><span role="heading" style="-webkit-box-orient: vertical; -webkit-line-clamp: 2; display: -webkit-box; overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; overflow-wrap: break-word; font-size: 16px; line-height: 24px; white-space-collapse: preserve;">what does source available licenses mean</span></div></div></div><div style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: flex; font-size: 12px; justify-content: end; line-height: 16px;"></div><div></div></div></div><div></div><div><div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div><div></div></div><div></div><div><div><div><div style="color: var(--m3c11,#eef0ff); position: relative; --m3c9: #e6e8f0; --m3c11: #e6e8f0; display: flex;"><div style="width: 652.438px;"><div><div style="display: contents;"></div></div><div dir="ltr" style="width: 652px; max-width: var(--CYi3c--fRcLaf,652px);"><div style="display: contents;"><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Source-available licenses</span>&nbsp;<mark style="border-radius: 4px; background-image: ; background-position-x: ; background-position-y: ; background-size: ; background-repeat: ; background-attachment: ; background-origin: ; background-clip: ; padding: 0px 2px;">allow you to download, view, and often modify a software project's code, but they impose specific&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">restrictions on how you use it</span></mark>. While they look like open-source because the code is public, they are legally distinct because they do not grant the "unrestricted freedom" required by the&nbsp;<span><a rel="noopener" href="https://opensource.org/osd" style="text-decoration-thickness: 1px; text-decoration-color: var(--JKqx2); -webkit-tap-highlight-color: rgba(255, 255, 255, 0.1); text-underline-offset: 1px; outline: 0px;">Open Source Definition</a></span>.<span><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span>&nbsp;</span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">Key Characteristics<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Source Code Visibility:</span>&nbsp;Users have full access to inspect and audit the code.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Usage Restrictions:</span>&nbsp;Unlike open source, these licenses typically include&nbsp;<span style="font-weight: 700;">"field-of-use" limitations</span>.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Frictionless Distribution:</span>&nbsp;Like open source, you usually don't have to "click-to-accept" a contract; the license is simply included with the download.</span><span><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; gap: 4px; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 85.0703px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">fossa.com</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+4</span></span></div></span></span></li></ul><div></div><div role="heading" style="margin-block: 24px 12px; font-family: var(--Aoh9Xe); font-size: var(--qpdFp); font-weight: var(--JT4IPc); line-height: var(--qYGXw); letter-spacing: 0px; color: var(--jINu6c);">Common Restrictions<span style="visibility: hidden;"><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span></span><span style="color: var(--IXoxUe); display: inline-block; transform: rotate(135deg);"><svg style="margin-top: 3px;" fill="currentColor" width="12px" height="12px" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24"><path d="M3.9 12c0-1.71 1.39-3.1 3.1-3.1h4V7H7c-2.76 0-5 2.24-5 5s2.24 5 5 5h4v-1.9H7c-1.71 0-3.1-1.39-3.1-3.1zM8 13h8v-2H8v2zm9-6h-4v1.9h4c1.71 0 3.1 1.39 3.1 3.1s-1.39 3.1-3.1 3.1h-4V17h4c2.76 0 5-2.24 5-5s-2.24-5-5-5z"></path></svg></span></span></span></div><div style="font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; overflow-wrap: break-word; margin-block: var(--xdqYEb--pNrv5d,12px) var(--xdqYEb--i8AQde,16px);">Companies typically use these to prevent "free-riding" by cloud giants who might otherwise resell their work as a managed service without contributing back.<span><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; gap: 4px; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 91.0078px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto, Arial, sans-serif; color: var(--IXoxUe); font-size: 11px; line-height: 1.45; display: flex; overflow: hidden; min-width: 0px;"><span style="overflow: hidden; text-overflow: ellipsis; min-width: 0px;">JustDo.com</span><span style="flex-shrink: 0;">&nbsp;+1</span></span></div></span></span></div><ul style="margin: 0px; padding: 0px; margin-block: 12px 16px; font-family: var(--nkmQOe); font-size: var(--z3BFIe); font-weight: var(--XWliwc); line-height: var(--a9X0Jc); letter-spacing: 0px; padding-inline-start: 16px;"><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Anti-Competition:</span>&nbsp;Prohibits using the software to build a competing product (e.g., you can't host it as a paid cloud service).</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Commercial Limitations:</span>&nbsp;Some only allow free use for non-production or non-commercial purposes, requiring a paid license for business use.</span></li><li style="margin: 0px 0px 12px; padding: 0px; list-style: disc; padding-inline-start: 4px;"><span style="overflow-wrap: break-word;"><span style="font-weight: 700;">Ethical/Niche Bans:</span>&nbsp;Restrictions against specific industries, such as forbidding use in nuclear facilities or by certain groups.</span><span><span style="position: relative; text-wrap: nowrap;"><span>&nbsp;</span><div style="align-items: center; display: flex; gap: 4px; height: 14px; overflow: hidden; width: 85.0703px;"><span style="font-family: &quot;Google Sans&quot;, Roboto,
